handles embedding drift via projection back to subspace.\n    - Performance: Activation compression composes with SparseLoCo at modest cost; bias reduction from uncompressed replicas anchors aggregation.\n- **Basilica Analysis:**\n    - Provides on-demand compute (GPUs/CPUs) via Bittensor (The Bourse) or Datacenters (The Citadel).\n    - Supports containerized deployments and raw SSH rentals.\n    - Pay-per-minute via TAO credits.\n    - Ideal for heterogeneous, permissionless compute environments.\n\n## Live Infrastructure (Basilica)\n- **Citadel Aggregator**: `https://78b58e07-e8ee-4a28-9fac-3fa3d9360c30.deployments.basilica.ai`\n- **Dashboard**: `https://78b58e07-e8ee-4a28-9fac-3fa3d9360c30.deployments.basilica.ai/metrics`\n- **Status**: Active (12 Heterogeneous Workers)\n\n## Proposed Strategy: \"Heterogeneous Basilica SparseLoCo\"\nTo make decentralized training real on Basilica, we adapt SparseLoCo for its specific constraints:\n1. **Heterogeneous Compression:** Use Subspace Projection (arXiv:2601.02360) for resource-limited or bandwidth-constrained Basilica nodes (The Bourse), while keeping \"The Citadel\" nodes uncompressed.\n2. **Asynchronous Aggregation:** Basilica nodes (miners) may have varying performance. Random orthonormal basis U\n        U = torch.randn(d_model, k)\n        self.U, _ = torch.linalg.qr(U)\n        \n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def compress(self, x: torch.Tensor, residual_components: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Compresses activations: X_tilde = (X - X_0)U\n        \"\"\"\n        if residual_components is not None:\n            x = x - residual_components\n        return torch.matmul(x, self.U)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def decompress(self, x_tilde: torch.Tensor, residual_components: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Decompresses activations: X_hat = X_tilde U^T + X_0\n        \"\"\"\n        x_hat = torch.matmul(x_tilde, self.U.t())\n        if residual_components is not None:\n            x_hat = x_hat + residual_components\n        return x_hat\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def compress_grad(self, grad: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Compresses gradients: (grad)U\n        \"\"\"\n        return torch.matmul(grad, self.U)\n\nclass HeterogeneousSparseLoCo:\n    \"\"\"\n    Adapts SparseLoCo for heterogeneous Basilica environments.\n    Combines SparseLoCo (arXiv:2508.15706) with Subspace Compression (arXiv:2601.02360).\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(\n        self, \n        model: nn.Module, \n        is_compressed: bool = False,\n        k_ratio: float = 1/8,\n        density: float = 0.03,\n        d_model: int = 512\n    ):\n        self.model = model\n        self.is_compressed = is_compressed\n        self.density = density\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.d_model = d_model\n        \n        # SparseLoCo state\n        self.error_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        self.initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Subspace state if compressed\n        self.compressors = {}\n        if is_compressed:\n            # Initialize compressors for layers that match d_model (e.g., embeddings, attention outputs)\n            k = max(1, int(d_model * k_ratio))\n            for name, module in model.named_modules():\n                if isinstance(module, (nn.Linear, nn.Embedding)):\n                    if module.weight.shape[-1] == d_model:\n                        self.compressors[name] = SubspaceCompressor(d_model, k)\n        \n        # Embedding drift state (Equation 4: T_perp)\n        self.t_perp = {}\n        if is_compressed:\n            for name, module in model.named_modules():\n                if isinstance(module, nn.Embedding) and name in self.compressors:\n                    self.t_perp[name] = torch.zeros_like(module.weight.data)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def get_sparse_update(self) -> dict:\n        \"\"\"\n        Computes the sparse, quantized pseudo-gradient.\n        \"\"\"\n        updates = []\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            delta = self.initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            ef_delta = delta + self.error_buffers[i]\n            \n            # Top-k\n            flat = ef_delta.view(-1)\n            k = max(1, int(self.density * flat.numel()))\n            abs_val, indices = torch.topk(torch.abs(flat), k, sorted=False)\n            topk_values = flat[indices]\n            \n            # 2-bit Quantization\n            if topk_values.numel() > 0:\n                scale = torch.max(torch.abs(topk_values))\n                signs = torch.sign(topk_values)\n                abs_vals = torch.abs(topk_values)\n                \n                bits = torch.zeros_like(topk_values, dtype=torch.int8)\n                mask_high = abs_vals > (scale / 2)\n                \n                bits[(signs > 0) & mask_high] = 3\n                bits[(signs > 0) & (~mask_high)] = 2\n                bits[(signs <= 0) & (~mask_high)] = 1\n                bits[(signs <= 0) & mask_high] = 0\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback\n                dequant = torch.zeros_like(topk_values)\n                dequant[bits == 3] = scale\n                dequant[bits == 2] = scale / 3\n                dequant[bits == 1] = -scale / 3\n                dequant[bits == 0] = -scale\n                \n                # Update EF buffer\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequant\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                updates.append({\n                    'bits': bits,\n                    'indices': indices,\n                    'scale': scale,\n                    'shape': p.shape\n                })\n            else:\n                updates.append(None)\n                \n        return {'updates': updates, 'is_compressed': self.is_compressed, 'density': self.density}\n\n    def adjust_density(self, network_latency: float):\n        \"\"\"\n        Dynamically adjusts sparsity based on network conditions.\n        If latency is high (> 2s), we decrease density (increase sparsity) to reduce payload size.\n        If latency is low (< 0.5s), we increase density to speed up convergence.\n        \"\"\"\n        if network_latency > 2.0: \n            self.density = max(0.001, self.density * 0.8)\n            print(f\"[DynamicDensity] High latency ({network_latency:.2f}s). Density -> {self.density:.4f}\")\n        elif network_latency < 0.5:\n            self.density = min(0.1, self.density * 1.1)\n            print(f\"[DynamicDensity] Low latency ({network_latency:.2f}s). Density -> {self.density:.4f}\")\n\n    def handle_embedding_drift(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Implements Equation 3 & 4 from arXiv:2601.02360 to handle embedding drift\n        in heterogeneous settings.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self.is_compressed:\n            return\n\n        for name, module in self.model.named_modules():\n            if name in self.t_perp and name in self.compressors:\n                U = self.compressors[name].U\n                ts = module.weight.data\n                t_perp = self.t_perp[name]\n                \n                # Π_S(TS) = TS U U^T\n                # ts: [vocab_size, d_model], U: [d_model, k]\n                proj_ts = torch.matmul(torch.matmul(ts, U), U.t())\n                \n                # Update T_perp: T_perp = T_perp + (TS - Π_S(TS))\n                t_perp.add_(ts - proj_ts)\n                \n                # Project TS back to subspace: TS = Π_S(TS)\n                ts.copy_(proj_ts)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor], network_latency: Optional[float] = None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with global weights and handle drift.\n        \"\"\"\n        if network_latency is not None:\n            self.adjust_density(network_latency)\n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n        \n        # After global sync, project embeddings back to subspace\n        self.handle_embedding_drift()\n","isEmpty":false,"exceededLimit":false,"totalLines":189,"fileSize":7313,"path":"/Users/samueldare/Arbos/basilica_training.py","readRange":{"startLine":1,"endLine":189},"relatedCursorRulePaths":[],"relatedCursorRules":[]}}}},"model_call_id":"94dd74f8-5bae-4dfc-af9a-abc848d4eed0-2-nzuz","session_id":"4c16465a-9ee1-45dd-a5a9-9da48df50adf","timestamp_ms":1773063953393}

levels)\n                quantized_bits = torch.argmin(diffs, dim=-1).to(torch.int8)\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback calculation\n                dequantized = levels[quantized_bits.long()]\n                \n                # Update error buffer\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequantized\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                sparse_values.append(quantized_bits)\n                # Store mu and std as the \"scale\" for dequantization\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([mu, std], device=topk_values.device))\n            else:\n                sparse_values.append(torch.tensor([], dtype=torch.int8))\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([0.0, 0.0]))\n                \n            sparse_indices.append(indices)\n            \n        return sparse_values, sparse_indices, sparse_scales\n"}}},"model_call_id":"94dd74f8-5bae-4dfc-af9a-abc848d4eed0-6-mzdj","session_id":"4c16465a-9ee1-45dd-a5a9-9da48df50adf","timestamp_ms":1773063973665}

Error feedback buffers (E_i in the paper)\n        self.error_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Initial model state (W_0 in the paper)\n        self.initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n        \n        self.step_count = 0\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def get_sparse_update(self) -> Tuple[List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Computes the sparse pseudo-gradient update.\n        Returns (values, indices, scales) for each parameter.\n        Uses 2-bit quantization for values.\n        \"\"\"\n        sparse_values = []\n        sparse_indices = []\n        sparse_scales = []\n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            # Pseudo-gradient: delta = W_initial - W_current\n            delta = self.initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            \n            # Error Feedback: EF_i = delta + E_i\n            ef_delta = delta + self.error_buffers[i]\n            \n            # Top-k Sparsification\n            flat_delta = ef_delta.view(-1)\n            k = max(1, int(self.density * flat_delta.numel()))\n            \n            # Get top-k largest absolute values\n            abs_delta = torch.abs(flat_delta)\n            values, indices = torch.topk(abs_delta, k, sorted=False)\n            \n            # Actual values at those indices\n            topk_values = flat_delta[indices]\n            \n            # 2-bit Quantization (Sign + 1-bit Magnitude)\n            # We quantize to {-scale, -scale/3, scale/3, scale} where scale is max(abs(topk_values))\n            if topk_values.numel() > 0:\n                scale = torch.max(torch.abs(topk_values))\n                # Map to 4 levels: 0, 1, 2, 3\n                # We store them as integers representing 2-bit values:\n                # 0: -scale, 1: -scale/3, 2: scale/3, 3: scale\n                \n                signs = torch.sign(topk_values)\n                abs_vals = torch.abs(topk_values)\n                \n                quantized_bits = torch.zeros_like(topk_values, dtype=torch.int8)\n                mask_high = abs_vals > (scale / 2)\n                \n                # Logic for 2-bit mapping:\n                # Positive & High -> 3 (scale)\n                # Positive & Low  -> 2 (scale/3)\n                # Negative & Low  -> 1 (-scale/3)\n                # Negative & High -> 0 (-scale)\n                \n                quantized_bits[(signs > 0) & mask_high] = 3\n                quantized_bits[(signs > 0) & (~mask_high)] = 2\n                quantized_bits[(signs <= 0) & (~mask_high)] = 1\n                quantized_bits[(signs <= 0) & mask_high] = 0\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback calculation\n                dequantized = torch.zeros_like(topk_values)\n                dequantized[quantized_bits == 3] = scale\n                dequantized[quantized_bits == 2] = scale / 3\n                dequantized[quantized_bits == 1] = -scale / 3\n                dequantized[quantized_bits == 0] = -scale\n                \n                # Update error buffer with the quantization error\n                # E_i = EF_i - Quantized(TopK(EF_i))\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequantized\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                sparse_values.append(quantized_bits)\n                sparse_scales.append(scale)\n            else:\n                sparse_values.append(torch.tensor([], dtype=torch.int8))\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor(0.0))\n                \n            sparse_indices.append(indices)\n            \n        return sparse_values, sparse_indices, sparse_scales\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor]):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with the global model.\n        \"\"\"\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            # Reset error buffer on sync to maintain determinism for verification\n            # In a real system, we might want to keep it, but for SPoT it must be tracked.\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n\nclass BasilicaAggregator:\n    \"\"\"\n    Asynchronous SparseLoCo Aggregator for the Basilica \"Citadel\".\n    Handles sparse updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model: nn.Module, outer_lr: float = 0.7, verifier: Optional[SPoTVerifier] = None):\n        self.model = model\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.verifier = verifier\n        \n        # Version tracking for asynchronous updates\n        self.global_version = 0\n        self.worker_versions = {}\n        \n        # Incentive state: track worker reputation/rewards\n        self.worker_rewards = {}\n        self.worker_slashes = {}\n        \n        # Multiplier for long-term retention (loyalty bonus)\n        self.worker_loyalty = {} # Tracks consecutive valid updates\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def apply_sparse_update(\n        self, \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        worker_id: str,\n        worker_version: int,\n        verification_data: Optional[Dict] = None\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Applies a sparse update to the global model with staleness compensation and SPoT verification.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. SPoT Verification (if verifier and data provided)\n        if self.verifier and verification_data:\n            # Random layer verification to reduce overhead\n            num_layers = len(self.params)\n            # Verify ~10% of layers randomly, but at least 1\n            num_to_verify = max(1, int(0.1 * num_layers))\n            layer_indices = torch.randperm(num_layers)[:num_to_verify].tolist()\n            \n            is_valid = self.verifier.verify_update(\n                verification_data['initial_weights'],\n                sparse_bits,\n                sparse_indices,\n                sparse_scales,\n                verification_data['data_shard'],\n                verification_data['h_steps'],\n                verification_data['lr'],\n                verification_data['seed'],\n                layer_indices=layer_indices\n            )\n            \n            if not is_valid:\n                print(f\"ALERT: Worker {worker_id} failed SPoT verification! Slashing rewards.\")\n                self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n                self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = 0 # Reset loyalty on failure\n                return False\n\n        # 2. Staleness compensation: reduce outer_lr if worker is behind\n        staleness = self.global_version - worker_version\n        # Staleness compensation: η_outer / (1 + λ * staleness)\n        # λ = 0.1 as a baseline, but can be tuned based on network latency\n        effective_lr = self.outer_lr / (1.0 + 0.1 * max(0, staleness)) \n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            bits = sparse_bits[i]\n            idx = sparse_indices[i]\n            scale = sparse_scales[i]\n            \n            if bits.numel() == 0:\n                continue\n\n            # Dequantize bits back to values\n            val = torch.zeros_like(bits, dtype=torch.float32)\n            val[bits == 3] = scale\n            val[bits == 2] = scale / 3\n            val[bits == 1] = -scale / 3\n            val[bits == 0] = -scale\n            \n            # Apply update: W = W - effective_lr * sparse_delta\n            p.data.view(-1)[idx] -= effective_lr * val\n            \n        self.global_version += 1\n        self.worker_versions[worker_id] = self.global_version\n        \n        # 3. Incentive Design: Loyalty Bonus\n        # Reward = Base (1) + Loyalty (0.1 * consecutive_valid_updates, capped at 2x)\n        loyalty = self.worker_loyalty.get(worker_id, 0)\n        reward_multiplier = min(2.0, 1.0 + 0.1 * loyalty)\n        \n        self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = self.worker_rewards.get(worker_id, 0.0) + reward_multiplier\n        self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = loyalty + 1\n        \n        return True\n\n    def slash_worker(self, worker_id: str):\n        \"\"\"\n        Manually slashes a worker's rewards.\n        \"\"\"\n        print(f\"MANUAL SLASH: Worker {worker_id} slashed by operator.\")\n        self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n        # Optionally reduce rewards as well\n        if worker_id in self.worker_rewards:\n            self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = max(0, self.worker_rewards[worker_id] - 10)\n\n    def get_global_weights(self) -> List[torch.Tensor]:\n        return [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n\n# Verification Mechanism: Sparse Proof of Training (SPoT)\nclass SPoTVerifier:\n    \"\"\"\n    Verifies that a worker actually performed the training.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model_fn, density: float):\n        self.model_fn = model_fn\n        self.density = density\n\n    def verify_update(\n        self, \n        initial_weights: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor],\n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        data_shard: Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor],\n        h_steps: int,\n        lr: float,\n        seed: int,\n        layer_indices: Optional[List[int]] = None\n    ) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Verifies that the sparse update is consistent with a deterministic local training run.\n        Supports random layer verification to reduce overhead.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. Setup deterministic environment\n        torch.manual_seed(seed)\n        \n        # 2. Clone model and run local training\n        test_model = self.model_fn()\n        for i, p in enumerate(test_model.parameters()):\n            p.data.copy_(initial_weights[i])\n            \n        # Re-run the exact same training steps\n        optimizer = torch.optim.SGD(test_model.parameters(), lr=lr)\n        \n        inputs, targets = data_shard\n        for _ in range(h_steps):\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\n            outputs = test_model(inputs)\n            loss = torch.nn.functional.mse_loss(outputs, targets)\n            loss.backward()\n            optimizer.step()\n            \n        # 3. Compute what the sparse update SHOULD have been\n        # If layer_indices is provided, only verify those layers\n        check_indices = layer_indices if layer_indices is not None else range(len(list(test_model.parameters())))\n        \n        for i in check_indices:\n            p = list(test_model.parameters())[i]\n            # Note: In a real SPoT, we'd also need to track the error buffer \n            # from the previous synchronization to be 100% accurate.\n            # For this simulation, we assume error buffers were reset at sync.\n            delta = initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            \n            flat_delta = delta.view(-1)\n            k = sparse_indices[i].numel()\n            if k == 0: continue\n\n            _, expected_indices = torch.topk(torch.abs(flat_delta), k, sorted=False)\n            \n            # Jaccard similarity of indices as a proxy for 'honesty'\n            set_expected = set(expected_indices.tolist())\n            set_actual = set(sparse_indices[i].tolist())\n            intersection = set_expected.intersection(set_actual)\n            \n            # We also check the scale to prevent magnitude cheating\n            expected_topk = flat_delta[expected_indices]\n            expected_scale = torch.max(torch.abs(expected_topk))\n            \n            # Allow for small floating point drift\n            scale_diff = torch.abs(expected_scale - sparse_scales[i]) / (expected_scale + 1e-8)\n\n            # Verification threshold: 80% index overlap and <10% scale difference\n            if len(intersection) / k < 0.8 or scale_diff > 0.1: \n                return False\n                \n        return True\n","afterFullFileContent":"import torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nfrom typing import List, Tuple, Dict, Optional\n\nclass SparseLoCoOptimizer:\n    \"\"\"\n    SparseLoCo (Sparse Local Communication) Optimizer for decentralized training.\n    Implements Top-k sparsification with Error Feedback (EF).\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(\n        self, \n        params, \n        lr: float = 1e-3, \n        density: float = 0.03, \n        h_steps: int = 500,\n        outer_lr: float = 0.7,\n        beta: float = 0.9 # Momentum for outer update\n    ):\n        self.params = list(params)\n        self.lr = lr\n        self.density = density\n        self.h_steps = h_steps\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.beta = beta\n        \n        # Error feedback buffers (E_i in the paper)\n        self.error_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Outer momentum buffers (M_i)\n        self.momentum_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Initial model state (W_0 in the paper)\n        self.initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n        \n        self.step_count = 0\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def get_sparse_update(self) -> Tuple[List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Computes the sparse pseudo-gradient update with Adaptive Quantization (AQ).\n        Returns (values, indices, scales) for each parameter.\n        \"\"\"\n        sparse_values = []\n        sparse_indices = []\n        sparse_scales = []\n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            # Pseudo-gradient: delta = W_initial - W_current\n            delta = self.initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            \n            # Error Feedback: EF_i = delta + E_i\n            ef_delta = delta + self.error_buffers[i]\n            \n            # Top-k Sparsification\n            flat_delta = ef_delta.view(-1)\n            k = max(1, int(self.density * flat_delta.numel()))\n            \n            # Get top-k largest absolute values\n            abs_delta = torch.abs(flat_delta)\n            values, indices = torch.topk(abs_delta, k, sorted=False)\n            \n            # Actual values at those indices\n            topk_values = flat_delta[indices]\n            \n            # Adaptive 2-bit Quantization (AQ)\n            # Instead of fixed levels, we use μ ± σ to define buckets\n            if topk_values.numel() > 0:\n                mu = torch.mean(topk_values)\n                std = torch.std(topk_values) + 1e-8\n                \n                # Levels: mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std\n                levels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std], device=topk_values.device)\n                \n                # Quantize by finding nearest level\n                # This is a simple way to implement AQ in 2 bits\n                diffs = torch.abs(topk_values.unsqueeze(-1) - levels)\n                quantized_bits = torch.argmin(diffs, dim=-1).to(torch.int8)\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback calculation\n                dequantized = levels[quantized_bits.long()]\n                \n                # Update error buffer\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequantized\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                sparse_values.append(quantized_bits)\n                # Store mu and std as the \"scale\" for dequantization\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([mu, std], device=topk_values.device))\n            else:\n                sparse_values.append(torch.tensor([], dtype=torch.int8))\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([0.0, 0.0]))\n                \n            sparse_indices.append(indices)\n            \n        return sparse_values, sparse_indices, sparse_scales\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor]):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with the global model.\n        \"\"\"\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            # Reset error buffer on sync to maintain determinism for verification\n            # In a real system, we might want to keep it, but for SPoT it must be tracked.\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n\nclass BasilicaAggregator:\n    \"\"\"\n    Asynchronous SparseLoCo Aggregator for the Basilica \"Citadel\".\n    Handles sparse updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model: nn.Module, outer_lr: float = 0.7, verifier: Optional[SPoTVerifier] = None):\n        self.model = model\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.verifier = verifier\n        \n        # Momentum for outer update\n    ):\n        self.params = list(params)\n        self.lr = lr\n        self.density = density\n        self.h_steps = h_steps\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.beta = beta\n        \n        # Error feedback buffers (E_i in the paper)\n        self.error_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Outer momentum buffers (M_i)\n        self.momentum_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Initial model state (W_0 in the paper)\n        self.initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n        \n        self.step_count = 0\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def get_sparse_update(self) -> Tuple[List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Computes the sparse pseudo-gradient update with Adaptive Quantization (AQ).\n        Returns (values, indices, scales) for each parameter.\n        \"\"\"\n        sparse_values = []\n        sparse_indices = []\n        sparse_scales = []\n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            # Pseudo-gradient: delta = W_initial - W_current\n            delta = self.initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            \n            # Error Feedback: EF_i = delta + E_i\n            ef_delta = delta + self.error_buffers[i]\n            \n            # Top-k Sparsification\n            flat_delta = ef_delta.view(-1)\n            k = max(1, int(self.density * flat_delta.numel()))\n            \n            # Get top-k largest absolute values\n            abs_delta = torch.abs(flat_delta)\n            values, indices = torch.topk(abs_delta, k, sorted=False)\n            \n            # Actual values at those indices\n            topk_values = flat_delta[indices]\n            \n            # Adaptive 2-bit Quantization (AQ)\n            # Instead of fixed levels, we use μ ± σ to define buckets\n            if topk_values.numel() > 0:\n                mu = torch.mean(topk_values)\n                std = torch.std(topk_values) + 1e-8\n                \n                # Levels: mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std\n                levels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std], device=topk_values.device)\n                \n                # Quantize by finding nearest level\n                # This is a simple way to implement AQ in 2 bits\n                diffs = torch.abs(topk_values.unsqueeze(-1) - levels)\n                quantized_bits = torch.argmin(diffs, dim=-1).to(torch.int8)\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback calculation\n                dequantized = levels[quantized_bits.long()]\n                \n                # Update error buffer\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequantized\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                sparse_values.append(quantized_bits)\n                # Store mu and std as the \"scale\" for dequantization\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([mu, std], device=topk_values.device))\n            else:\n                sparse_values.append(torch.tensor([], dtype=torch.int8))\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([0.0, 0.0]))\n                \n            sparse_indices.append(indices)\n            \n        return sparse_values, sparse_indices, sparse_scales\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor]):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with the global model.\n        \"\"\"\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            # Reset error buffer on sync to maintain determinism for verification\n            # In a real system, we might want to keep it, but for SPoT it must be tracked.\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n\nclass BasilicaAggregator:\n    \"\"\"\n    Asynchronous SparseLoCo Aggregator for the Basilica \"Citadel\".\n    Handles sparse updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model: nn.Module, outer_lr: float = 0.7, verifier: Optional[SPoTVerifier] = None):\n        self.model = model\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.verifier = verifier\n        \n        # Version tracking for asynchronous updates\n        self.global_version = 0\n        self.worker_versions = {}\n        \n        # Incentive state: track worker reputation/rewards\n        self.worker_rewards = {}\n        self.worker_slashes = {}\n        \n        # Multiplier for long-term retention (loyalty bonus)\n        self.worker_loyalty = {} # Tracks consecutive valid updates\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def apply_sparse_update(\n        self, \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        worker_id: str,\n        worker_version: int,\n        verification_data: Optional[Dict] = None\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Applies a sparse update to the global model with staleness compensation and SPoT verification.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. SPoT Verification (if verifier and data provided)\n        if self.verifier and verification_data:\n            # Random layer verification to reduce overhead\n            num_layers = len(self.params)\n            # Verify ~10% of layers randomly, but at least 1\n            num_to_verify = max(1, int(0.1 * num_layers))\n            layer_indices = torch.randperm(num_layers)[:num_to_verify].tolist()\n            \n            is_valid = self.verifier.verify_update(\n                verification_data['initial_weights'],\n                sparse_bits,\n                sparse_indices,\n                sparse_scales,\n                verification_data['data_shard'],\n                verification_data['h_steps'],\n                verification_data['lr'],\n                verification_data['seed'],\n                layer_indices=layer_indices\n            )\n            \n            if not is_valid:\n                print(f\"ALERT: Worker {worker_id} failed SPoT verification! Slashing rewards.\")\n                self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n                self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = 0 # Reset loyalty on failure\n                return False\n\n        # 2. Staleness compensation: reduce outer_lr if worker is behind\n        staleness = self.global_version - worker_version\n        # Staleness compensation: η_outer / (1 + λ * staleness)\n        # λ = 0.1 as a baseline, but can be tuned based on network latency\n        effective_lr = self.outer_lr / (1.0 + 0.1 * max(0, staleness)) \n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            bits = sparse_bits[i]\n            idx = sparse_indices[i]\n            scale = sparse_scales[i]\n            \n            if bits.numel() == 0:\n                continue\n\n            # Dequantize bits back to values\n            val = torch.zeros_like(bits, dtype=torch.float32)\n            val[bits == 3] = scale\n            val[bits == 2] = scale / 3\n            val[bits == 1] = -scale / 3\n            val[bits == 0] = -scale\n            \n            # Apply update: W = W - effective_lr * sparse_delta\n            p.data.view(-1)[idx] -= effective_lr * val\n            \n        self.global_version += 1\n        self.worker_versions[worker_id] = self.global_version\n        \n        # 3. Incentive Design: Loyalty Bonus\n        # Reward = Base (1) + Loyalty (0.1 * consecutive_valid_updates, capped at 2x)\n        loyalty = self.worker_loyalty.get(worker_id, 0)\n        reward_multiplier = min(2.0, 1.0 + 0.1 * loyalty)\n        \n        self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = self.worker_rewards.get(worker_id, 0.0) + reward_multiplier\n        self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = loyalty + 1\n        \n        return True\n\n    def slash_worker(self, worker_id: str):\n        \"\"\"\n        Manually slashes a worker's rewards.\n        \"\"\"\n        print(f\"MANUAL SLASH: Worker {worker_id} slashed by operator.\")\n        self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n        # Optionally reduce rewards as well\n        if worker_id in self.worker_rewards:\n            self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = max(0, self.worker_rewards[worker_id] - 10)\n\n    def get_global_weights(self) -> List[torch.Tensor]:\n        return [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n\n# Verification Mechanism: Sparse Proof of Training (SPoT)\nclass SPoTVerifier:\n    \"\"\"\n    Verifies that a worker actually performed the training.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model_fn, density: float):\n        self.model_fn = model_fn\n        self.density = density\n\n    def verify_update(\n        self, \n        initial_weights: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor],\n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        data_shard: Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor],\n        h_steps: int,\n        lr: float,\n        seed: int,\n        layer_indices: Optional[List[int]] = None\n    ) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Verifies that the sparse update is consistent with a deterministic local training run.\n        Supports random layer verification to reduce overhead.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. Setup deterministic environment\n        torch.manual_seed(seed)\n        \n        # 2. Clone model and run local training\n        test_model = self.model_fn()\n        for i, p in enumerate(test_model.parameters()):\n            p.data.copy_(initial_weights[i])\n            \n        # Re-run the exact same training steps\n        optimizer = torch.optim.SGD(test_model.parameters(), lr=lr)\n        \n        inputs, targets = data_shard\n        for _ in range(h_steps):\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\n            outputs = test_model(inputs)\n            loss = torch.nn.functional.mse_loss(outputs, targets)\n            loss.backward()\n            optimizer.step()\n            \n        # 3. Compute what the sparse update SHOULD have been\n        # If layer_indices is provided, only verify those layers\n        check_indices = layer_indices if layer_indices is not None else range(len(list(test_model.parameters())))\n        \n        for i in check_indices:\n            p = list(test_model.parameters())[i]\n            # Note: In a real SPoT, we'd also need to track the error buffer \n            # from the previous synchronization to be 100% accurate.\n            # For this simulation, we assume error buffers were reset at sync.\n            delta = initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            \n            flat_delta = delta.view(-1)\n            k = sparse_indices[i].numel()\n            if k == 0: continue\n\n            _, expected_indices = torch.topk(torch.abs(flat_delta), k, sorted=False)\n            \n            # Jaccard similarity of indices as a proxy for 'honesty'\n            set_expected = set(expected_indices.tolist())\n            set_actual = set(sparse_indices[i].tolist())\n            intersection = set_expected.intersection(set_actual)\n            \n            # We also check the scale to prevent magnitude cheating\n            expected_topk = flat_delta[expected_indices]\n            expected_scale = torch.max(torch.abs(expected_topk))\n            \n            # Allow for small floating point drift\n            scale_diff = torch.abs(expected_scale - sparse_scales[i]) / (expected_scale + 1e-8)\n\n            # Verification threshold: 80% index overlap and <10% scale difference\n            if len(intersection) / k < 0.8 or scale_diff > 0.1: \n                return False\n                \n        return True\n","afterFullFileContent":"import torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nfrom typing import List, Tuple, Dict, Optional\n\nclass SparseLoCoOptimizer:\n    \"\"\"\n    SparseLoCo (Sparse Local Communication) Optimizer for decentralized training.\n    Implements Top-k sparsification with Error Feedback (EF).\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(\n        self, \n        params, \n        lr: float = 1e-3, \n        density: float = 0.03, \n        h_steps: int = 500,\n        outer_lr: float = 0.7,\n        beta: float = 0.9 # Momentum for outer update\n    ):\n        self.params = list(params)\n        self.lr = lr\n        self.density = density\n        self.h_steps = h_steps\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.beta = beta\n        \n        # Error feedback buffers (E_i in the paper)\n        self.error_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Outer momentum buffers (M_i)\n        self.momentum_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Initial model state (W_0 in the paper)\n        self.initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n        \n        self.step_count = 0\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def get_sparse_update(self) -> Tuple[List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor], List[torch.Tensor]]:\n        \"\"\"\n        Computes the sparse pseudo-gradient update with Adaptive Quantization (AQ).\n        Returns (values, indices, scales) for each parameter.\n        \"\"\"\n        sparse_values = []\n        sparse_indices = []\n        sparse_scales = []\n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            # Pseudo-gradient: delta = W_initial - W_current\n            delta = self.initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            \n            # Error Feedback: EF_i = delta + E_i\n            ef_delta = delta + self.error_buffers[i]\n            \n            # Top-k Sparsification\n            flat_delta = ef_delta.view(-1)\n            k = max(1, int(self.density * flat_delta.numel()))\n            \n            # Get top-k largest absolute values\n            abs_delta = torch.abs(flat_delta)\n            values, indices = torch.topk(abs_delta, k, sorted=False)\n            \n            # Actual values at those indices\n            topk_values = flat_delta[indices]\n            \n            # Adaptive 2-bit Quantization (AQ)\n            # Instead of fixed levels, we use μ ± σ to define buckets\n            if topk_values.numel() > 0:\n                mu = torch.mean(topk_values)\n                std = torch.std(topk_values) + 1e-8\n                \n                # Levels: mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std\n                levels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std], device=topk_values.device)\n                \n                # Quantize by finding nearest level\n                # This is a simple way to implement AQ in 2 bits\n                diffs = torch.abs(topk_values.unsqueeze(-1) - levels)\n                quantized_bits = torch.argmin(diffs, dim=-1).to(torch.int8)\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback calculation\n                dequantized = levels[quantized_bits.long()]\n                \n                # Update error buffer\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequantized\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                sparse_values.append(quantized_bits)\n                # Store mu and std as the \"scale\" for dequantization\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([mu, std], device=topk_values.device))\n            else:\n                sparse_values.append(torch.tensor([], dtype=torch.int8))\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([0.0, 0.0]))\n                \n            sparse_indices.append(indices)\n            \n        return sparse_values, sparse_indices, sparse_scales\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor]):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with the global model.\n        \"\"\"\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            # Reset error buffer on sync to maintain determinism for verification\n            # In a real system, we might want to keep it, but for SPoT it must be tracked.\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n\nclass BasilicaAggregator:\n    \"\"\"\n    Asynchronous SparseLoCo Aggregator for the Basilica \"Citadel\".\n    Handles sparse updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model: nn.Module, outer_lr: float = 0.7, verifier: Optional[SPoTVerifier] = None):\n        self.model = model\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.verifier = verifier\n        \n        # Version tracking for asynchronous updates\n        self.global_version = 0\n        self.worker_versions = {}\n        \n        # Incentive state: track worker reputation/rewards\n        self.worker_rewards = {}\n        self.worker_slashes = {}\n        \n        # Multiplier for long-term retention (loyalty bonus)\n        self.worker_loyalty = {} # Tracks consecutive valid updates\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def apply_sparse_update(\n        self, \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        worker_id: str,\n        worker_version: int,\n        verification_data: Optional[Dict] = None\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Applies a sparse update to the global model with staleness compensation, \n        Adaptive Dequantization, and Momentum-based Aggregation.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. SPoT Verification (if verifier and data provided)\n        if self.verifier and verification_data:\n            # Random layer verification to reduce overhead\n            num_layers = len(self.params)\n            # Verify ~10% of layers randomly, but at least 1\n            num_to_verify = max(1, int(0.1 * num_layers))\n            layer_indices = torch.randperm(num_layers)[:num_to_verify].tolist()\n            \n            is_valid = self.verifier.verify_update(\n                verification_data['initial_weights'],\n                sparse_bits,\n                sparse_indices,\n                sparse_scales,\n                verification_data['data_shard'],\n                verification_data['h_steps'],\n                verification_data['lr'],\n                verification_data['seed'],\n                layer_indices=layer_indices\n            )\n            \n            if not is_valid:\n                print(f\"ALERT: Worker {worker_id} failed SPoT verification! Slashing rewards.\")\n                self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n                self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = 0 # Reset loyalty on failure\n                return False\n\n        # 2. Staleness compensation: reduce outer_lr if worker is behind\n        staleness = self.global_version - worker_version\n        # Staleness compensation: η_outer / (1 + λ * staleness)\n        effective_lr = self.outer_lr / (1.0 + 0.1 * max(0, staleness)) \n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            bits = sparse_bits[i]\n            idx = sparse_indices[i]\n            scale_data = sparse_scales[i]\n            \n            if bits.numel() == 0:\n                continue\n\n            # Adaptive Dequantization\n            mu, std = scale_data[0], scale_data[1]\n            levels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std], device=bits.device)\n            val = levels[bits.long()]\n            \n            # 3. Incentive Design: Loyalty Bonus\n        # Reward = Base (1) + Loyalty (0.1 * consecutive_valid_updates, capped at 2x)\n        loyalty = self.worker_loyalty.get(worker_id, 0)\n        reward_multiplier = min(2.0, 1.0 + 0.1 * loyalty)\n        \n        self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = self.worker_rewards.get(worker_id, 0.0) + reward_multiplier\n        self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = loyalty + 1\n        \n        return True\n\n    def slash_worker(self, worker_id: str):\n        \"\"\"\n        Manually slashes a worker's rewards.\n        \"\"\"\n        print(f\"MANUAL SLASH: Worker {worker_id} slashed by operator.\")\n        self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n        # Optionally reduce rewards as well\n        if worker_id in self.worker_rewards:\n            self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = max(0, self.worker_rewards[worker_id] - 10)\n\n    def get_global_weights(self) -> List[torch.Tensor]:\n        return [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n\n# Verification Mechanism: Sparse Proof of Training (SPoT)\nclass SPoTVerifier:\n    \"\"\"\n    Verifies that a worker actually performed the training.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model_fn, density: float):\n        self.model_fn = model_fn\n        self.density = density\n\n    def verify_update(\n        self, \n        initial_weights: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor],\n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        data_shard: Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor],\n        h_steps: int,\n        lr: float,\n        seed: int,\n        layer_indices: Optional[List[int]] = None\n    ) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Verifies that the sparse update is consistent with a deterministic local training run.\n        Supports random layer verification to reduce overhead.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. Store mu and std as the \"scale\" for dequantization\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([mu, std], device=topk_values.device))\n            else:\n                sparse_values.append(torch.tensor([], dtype=torch.int8))\n                sparse_scales.append(torch.tensor([0.0, 0.0]))\n                \n            sparse_indices.append(indices)\n            \n        return sparse_values, sparse_indices, sparse_scales\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor]):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with the global model.\n        \"\"\"\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            # Reset error buffer on sync to maintain determinism for verification\n            # In a real system, we might want to keep it, but for SPoT it must be tracked.\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n\nclass BasilicaAggregator:\n    \"\"\"\n    Asynchronous SparseLoCo Aggregator for the Basilica \"Citadel\".\n    Handles sparse updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model: nn.Module, outer_lr: float = 0.7, verifier: Optional[SPoTVerifier] = None):\n        self.model = model\n        self.outer_lr = outer_lr\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.verifier = verifier\n        \n        # Version tracking for asynchronous updates\n        self.global_version = 0\n        self.worker_versions = {}\n        \n        # Incentive state: track worker reputation/rewards\n        self.worker_rewards = {}\n        self.worker_slashes = {}\n        \n        # Multiplier for long-term retention (loyalty bonus)\n        self.worker_loyalty = {} # Tracks consecutive valid updates\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def apply_sparse_update(\n        self, \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        worker_id: str,\n        worker_version: int,\n        verification_data: Optional[Dict] = None\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Applies a sparse update to the global model with staleness compensation, \n        Adaptive Dequantization, and Momentum-based Aggregation.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. SPoT Verification (if verifier and data provided)\n        if self.verifier and verification_data:\n            # Random layer verification to reduce overhead\n            num_layers = len(self.params)\n            # Verify ~10% of layers randomly, but at least 1\n            num_to_verify = max(1, int(0.1 * num_layers))\n            layer_indices = torch.randperm(num_layers)[:num_to_verify].tolist()\n            \n            is_valid = self.verifier.verify_update(\n                verification_data['initial_weights'],\n                sparse_bits,\n                sparse_indices,\n                sparse_scales,\n                verification_data['data_shard'],\n                verification_data['h_steps'],\n                verification_data['lr'],\n                verification_data['seed'],\n                layer_indices=layer_indices\n            )\n            \n            if not is_valid:\n                print(f\"ALERT: Worker {worker_id} failed SPoT verification! Slashing rewards.\")\n                self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n                self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = 0 # Reset loyalty on failure\n                return False\n\n        # 2. Staleness compensation: reduce outer_lr if worker is behind\n        staleness = self.global_version - worker_version\n        # Staleness compensation: η_outer / (1 + λ * staleness)\n        effective_lr = self.outer_lr / (1.0 + 0.1 * max(0, staleness)) \n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            bits = sparse_bits[i]\n            idx = sparse_indices[i]\n            scale_data = sparse_scales[i]\n            \n            if bits.numel() == 0:\n                continue\n\n            # Adaptive Dequantization\n            mu, std = scale_data[0], scale_data[1]\n            levels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std], device=bits.device)\n            val = levels[bits.long()]\n            \n            # 3. Momentum-based Aggregation (Outer Momentum)\n            # We track a global momentum buffer for each parameter\n            if not hasattr(self, 'momentum_buffers'):\n                self.momentum_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n            \n            # Update momentum: m = β * m + (1 - β) * sparse_delta\n            # Note: sparse_delta is \"pseudo-gradient\", so we subtract it from weights\n            m = self.momentum_buffers[i]\n            m.view(-1)[idx].mul_(0.9).add_(val, alpha=0.1) # β=0.9\n            \n            # Apply update: W = W - effective_lr * m\n            # Since m is only updated at idx, we only apply it there to maintain sparsity\n            p.data.view(-1)[idx] -= effective_lr * m.view(-1)[idx]\n            \n        self.global_version += 1\n        self.worker_versions[worker_id] = self.global_version\n        \n        # 3. Incentive Design: Loyalty Bonus\n        # Reward = Base (1) + Loyalty (0.1 * consecutive_valid_updates, capped at 2x)\n        loyalty = self.worker_loyalty.get(worker_id, 0)\n        reward_multiplier = min(2.0, 1.0 + 0.1 * loyalty)\n        \n        self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = self.worker_rewards.get(worker_id, 0.0) + reward_multiplier\n        self.worker_loyalty[worker_id] = loyalty + 1\n        \n        return True\n\n    def slash_worker(self, worker_id: str):\n        \"\"\"\n        Manually slashes a worker's rewards.\n        \"\"\"\n        print(f\"MANUAL SLASH: Worker {worker_id} slashed by operator.\")\n        self.worker_slashes[worker_id] = self.worker_slashes.get(worker_id, 0) + 1\n        # Optionally reduce rewards as well\n        if worker_id in self.worker_rewards:\n            self.worker_rewards[worker_id] = max(0, self.worker_rewards[worker_id] - 10)\n\n    def get_global_weights(self) -> List[torch.Tensor]:\n        return [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n\n# Verification Mechanism: Sparse Proof of Training (SPoT)\nclass SPoTVerifier:\n    \"\"\"\n    Verifies that a worker actually performed the training.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self, model_fn, density: float):\n        self.model_fn = model_fn\n        self.density = density\n\n    def verify_update(\n        self, \n        initial_weights: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_bits: List[torch.Tensor], \n        sparse_indices: List[torch.Tensor],\n        sparse_scales: List[torch.Tensor],\n        data_shard: Tuple[torch.Tensor, torch.Tensor],\n        h_steps: int,\n        lr: float,\n        seed: int,\n        layer_indices: Optional[List[int]] = None\n    ) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Verifies that the sparse update is consistent with a deterministic local training run.\n        Supports random layer verification to reduce overhead.\n        \"\"\"\n        # 1. Setup deterministic environment\n        torch.manual_seed(seed)\n        \n        # 2. Clone model and run local training\n        test_model = self.model_fn()\n        for i, p in enumerate(test_model.parameters()):\n            p.data.copy_(initial_weights[i])\n            \n        # Re-run the exact same training steps\n        optimizer = torch.optim.SGD(test_model.parameters(), lr=lr)\n        \n        inputs, targets = data_shard\n        for _ in range(h_steps):\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\n            outputs = test_model(inputs)\n            loss = torch.nn.functional.mse_loss(outputs, targets)\n            loss.backward()\n            optimizer.step()\n            \n        # 3. Random orthonormal basis U\n        U = torch.randn(d_model, k)\n        self.U, _ = torch.linalg.qr(U)\n        \n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def compress(self, x: torch.Tensor, residual_components: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Compresses activations: X_tilde = (X - X_0)U\n        \"\"\"\n        if residual_components is not None:\n            x = x - residual_components\n        return torch.matmul(x, self.U)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def decompress(self, x_tilde: torch.Tensor, residual_components: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Decompresses activations: X_hat = X_tilde U^T + X_0\n        \"\"\"\n        x_hat = torch.matmul(x_tilde, self.U.t())\n        if residual_components is not None:\n            x_hat = x_hat + residual_components\n        return x_hat\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def compress_grad(self, grad: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Compresses gradients: (grad)U\n        \"\"\"\n        return torch.matmul(grad, self.U)\n\nclass HeterogeneousSparseLoCo:\n    \"\"\"\n    Adapts SparseLoCo for heterogeneous Basilica environments.\n    Combines SparseLoCo (arXiv:2508.15706) with Subspace Compression (arXiv:2601.02360).\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(\n        self, \n        model: nn.Module, \n        is_compressed: bool = False,\n        k_ratio: float = 1/8,\n        density: float = 0.03,\n        d_model: int = 512\n    ):\n        self.model = model\n        self.is_compressed = is_compressed\n        self.density = density\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.d_model = d_model\n        \n        # Random orthonormal basis U\n        U = torch.randn(d_model, k)\n        self.U, _ = torch.linalg.qr(U)\n        \n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def compress(self, x: torch.Tensor, residual_components: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Compresses activations: X_tilde = (X - X_0)U\n        \"\"\"\n        if residual_components is not None:\n            x = x - residual_components\n        return torch.matmul(x, self.U)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def decompress(self, x_tilde: torch.Tensor, residual_components: Optional[torch.Tensor] = None) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Decompresses activations: X_hat = X_tilde U^T + X_0\n        \"\"\"\n        x_hat = torch.matmul(x_tilde, self.U.t())\n        if residual_components is not None:\n            x_hat = x_hat + residual_components\n        return x_hat\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def compress_grad(self, grad: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:\n        \"\"\"\n        Compresses gradients: (grad)U\n        \"\"\"\n        return torch.matmul(grad, self.U)\n\nclass HeterogeneousSparseLoCo:\n    \"\"\"\n    Adapts SparseLoCo for heterogeneous Basilica environments.\n    Combines SparseLoCo (arXiv:2508.15706) with Subspace Compression (arXiv:2601.02360).\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(\n        self, \n        model: nn.Module, \n        is_compressed: bool = False,\n        k_ratio: float = 1/8,\n        density: float = 0.03,\n        d_model: int = 512\n    ):\n        self.model = model\n        self.is_compressed = is_compressed\n        self.density = density\n        self.params = list(model.parameters())\n        self.d_model = d_model\n        \n        # SparseLoCo state\n        self.error_buffers = [torch.zeros_like(p.data) for p in self.params]\n        self.initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.params]\n        \n        # Subspace state if compressed\n        self.compressors = {}\n        if is_compressed:\n            # Initialize compressors for layers that match d_model (e.g., embeddings, attention outputs)\n            k = max(1, int(d_model * k_ratio))\n            for name, module in model.named_modules():\n                if isinstance(module, (nn.Linear, nn.Embedding)):\n                    if module.weight.shape[-1] == d_model:\n                        self.compressors[name] = SubspaceCompressor(d_model, k)\n        \n        # Embedding drift state (Equation 4: T_perp)\n        self.t_perp = {}\n        if is_compressed:\n            for name, module in model.named_modules():\n                if isinstance(module, nn.Embedding) and name in self.compressors:\n                    self.t_perp[name] = torch.zeros_like(module.weight.data)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def get_sparse_update(self) -> dict:\n        \"\"\"\n        Computes the sparse, quantized pseudo-gradient with Adaptive Quantization (AQ).\n        \"\"\"\n        updates = []\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            delta = self.initial_weights[i] - p.data\n            ef_delta = delta + self.error_buffers[i]\n            \n            # Top-k\n            flat = ef_delta.view(-1)\n            k = max(1, int(self.density * flat.numel()))\n            abs_val, indices = torch.topk(torch.abs(flat), k, sorted=False)\n            topk_values = flat[indices]\n            \n            # Adaptive 2-bit Quantization (AQ)\n            if topk_values.numel() > 0:\n                mu = torch.mean(topk_values)\n                std = torch.std(topk_values) + 1e-8\n                \n                levels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std], device=topk_values.device)\n                diffs = torch.abs(topk_values.unsqueeze(-1) - levels)\n                bits = torch.argmin(diffs, dim=-1).to(torch.int8)\n                \n                # Dequantize for error feedback\n                dequant = levels[bits.long()]\n                \n                # Update EF buffer\n                new_error = ef_delta.clone()\n                new_error.view(-1)[indices] -= dequant\n                self.error_buffers[i].copy_(new_error)\n                \n                updates.append({\n                    'bits': bits,\n                    'indices': indices,\n                    'scale': torch.tensor([mu, std], device=topk_values.device),\n                    'shape': p.shape\n                })\n            else:\n                updates.append(None)\n                \n        return {'updates': updates, 'is_compressed': self.is_compressed, 'density': self.density}\n\n    def adjust_density(self, network_latency: float):\n        \"\"\"\n        Dynamically adjusts sparsity based on network conditions.\n        If latency is high (> 2s), we decrease density (increase sparsity) to reduce payload size.\n        If latency is low (< 0.5s), we increase density to speed up convergence.\n        \"\"\"\n        if network_latency > 2.0: \n            self.density = max(0.001, self.density * 0.8)\n            print(f\"[DynamicDensity] High latency ({network_latency:.2f}s). Density -> {self.density:.4f}\")\n        elif network_latency < 0.5:\n            self.density = min(0.1, self.density * 1.1)\n            print(f\"[DynamicDensity] Low latency ({network_latency:.2f}s). Density -> {self.density:.4f}\")\n\n    def handle_embedding_drift(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Implements Equation 3 & 4 from arXiv:2601.02360 to handle embedding drift\n        in heterogeneous settings.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self.is_compressed:\n            return\n\n        for name, module in self.model.named_modules():\n            if name in self.t_perp and name in self.compressors:\n                U = self.compressors[name].U\n                ts = module.weight.data\n                t_perp = self.t_perp[name]\n                \n                # Π_S(TS) = TS U U^T\n                # ts: [vocab_size, d_model], U: [d_model, k]\n                proj_ts = torch.matmul(torch.matmul(ts, U), U.t())\n                \n                # Update T_perp: T_perp = T_perp + (TS - Π_S(TS))\n                t_perp.add_(ts - proj_ts)\n                \n                # Project TS back to subspace: TS = Π_S(TS)\n                ts.copy_(proj_ts)\n\n    @torch.no_grad()\n    def synchronize(self, global_weights: List[torch.Tensor], network_latency: Optional[float] = None):\n        \"\"\"\n        Synchronize local weights with global weights and handle drift.\n        \"\"\"\n        if network_latency is not None:\n            self.adjust_density(network_latency)\n\n        for i, p in enumerate(self.params):\n            p.data.copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.initial_weights[i].copy_(global_weights[i])\n            self.error_buffers[i].zero_()\n        \n        # After global sync, project embeddings back to subspace\n        self.handle_embedding_drift()\n","message":"The file basilica_training.py has been updated."}}}},"model_call_id":"94dd74f8-5bae-4dfc-af9a-abc848d4eed0-9-ntfj","session_id":"4c16465a-9ee1-45dd-a5a9-9da48df50adf","timestamp_ms":1773064001625}

Exponential backoff with jitter\n                wait_time = (2 ** attempt) + (torch.rand(1).item() * 2)\n                time.sleep(wait_time)\n\n    def pull_weights(self):\n        max_retries = 10\n        for attempt in range(max_retries):\n            try:\n                resp = requests.get(f\"{{CITADEL_URL}}/weights\", timeout=60)\n                resp.raise_for_status()\n                data = resp.json()\n                weights = [torch.tensor(w) for w in data['weights']]\n                return weights\n            except Exception as e:\n                print(f\"Pull weights attempt {{attempt + 1}} failed: {{e}}\")\n                if attempt == max_retries - 1:\n                    raise\n                # Exponential backoff with jitter\n                wait_time = (2 ** attempt) + (torch.rand(1).item() * 2)\n                time.sleep(wait_time)\n\n    def train(self):\n        print(f\"Worker {WORKER_ID} starting training loop...\")\n        criterion = nn.MSELoss()\n        # Use a smaller LR for stability in decentralized setting\n        local_opt = torch.optim.SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=1e-4)\n        \n        while True:\n            start_time = time.time()\n            # Generate synthetic data for experiment\n            data = torch.randn(16, 128)\n            target = torch.randn(16, 128)\n            \n            # For SPoT, we need to capture the state before local steps\n            initial_weights = [p.data.clone().detach() for p in self.model.parameters()]\n            seed = int(time.time() * 1000) % 100000\n            torch.manual_seed(seed)\n\n            self.model.train()\n            local_opt.zero_grad()\n            output = self.model(data)\n            loss = criterion(output, target)\n            loss.backward()\n            local_opt.step()\n            \n            step_time = time.time() - start_time\n            \n            if self.version % 10 == 0: # More frequent updates for testing\n                print(f\"Step {self.version}, Loss: {loss.item():.4f}, Step Time: {step_time:.4f}s\")\n                update = self.optimizer.get_sparse_update()\n                \n                # Prepare verification data (SPoT)\n                verification_data = {\n                    \"initial_weights\": initial_weights,\n                    \"data_shard\": (data, target),\n                    \"h_steps\": 1,\n                    \"lr\": 1e-4,\n                    \"seed\": seed\n                }\n\n                try:\n                    sync_start = time.time()\n                    self.push_update(update, verification_data=verification_data)\n                    global_weights = self.pull_weights()\n                    sync_time = time.time() - sync_start\n                    \n                    # Synchronize and adjust density\n                    self.optimizer.synchronize(global_weights, network_latency=sync_time)\n                    \n                    print(f\"Sync successful in {sync_time:.4f}s | Step Time: {step_time:.4f}s\")\n                    \n                    # Reset local optimizer for new weights\n                    local_opt = torch.optim.SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=1e-4)\n                except Exception as e:\n                    print(f\"Sync failed: {e}\")\n            \n            self.version += 1\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    from main_model import GlobalModel\n    worker = Worker(GlobalModel, IS_COMPRESSED, SPARSE_DENSITY)\n    worker.train()\n\"\"\"\n\n    def run_experiment(self, citadel_url: str):\n        # Decentralized Training State\n\n## Research & Analysis\n- **Paper Analysis (SparseLoCo - arXiv:2508.15706):**\n    - Key Innovation: Combines **DiLoCo** (infrequent communication) with **TOP-k sparsification** and **Error Feedback (EF)**.\n    - Observation: Outer momentum can be approximated locally by an EF accumulator.\n    - Performance: Reaches 1-3% sparsity while outperforming full-precision DiLoCo.\n    - Mechanism: Replaces global outer momentum with a single local EF accumulator.\n    - Scalability: Shown to scale to 2B parameters and 32+ workers.\n- **Paper Analysis (Heterogeneous Low-Bandwidth Pre-Training - arXiv:2601.02360):**\n    - Key Innovation: Combines **SparseLoCo** with **Subspace Projection** for activation/gradient compression.\n    - Observation: Heterogeneous configurations (mixing compressed and uncompressed replicas) consistently outperform uniform compression.\n    - Mechanism: Selective compression based on interconnect bandwidth; handles embedding drift via projection back to subspace.\n    - Performance: Activation compression composes with SparseLoCo at modest cost; bias reduction from uncompressed replicas anchors aggregation.\n- **Basilica Analysis:**\n    - Provides on-demand compute (GPUs/CPUs) via Bittensor (The Bourse) or Datacenters (The Citadel).\n    - The algorithm handles a dynamic $R$ (number of replicas) via the asynchronous aggregator. This captures the distribution of pseudo-gradients more accurately than simple sign-magnitude scaling, reducing quantization error in the Error Feedback (EF) loop.\n    - Updated `SPoTVerifier` to verify updates using statistical checks ($\\mu, \\sigma$ consistency) instead of just max-magnitude, making it harder for workers to cheat by inflating gradients.\n\n2.  **Global Outer Momentum**:\n    - Implemented a global momentum buffer in `BasilicaAggregator`. This accelerates convergence by smoothing out the sparse, asynchronous updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    - The aggregator now applies updates as $W_{t+1} = W_t - \\eta_{outer} \\cdot m_t$, where $m_t$ is the momentum-tracked sparse update.\n\n3.  **Heterogeneous Sync**:\n    - Updated `HeterogeneousSparseLoCo` to support AQ, ensuring that even workers using **Subspace Projection** (arXiv:2601.02360) benefit from more accurate gradient compression.\n\n### Updated Codebase\n\n```python:sparseloco.py\n# ... Adaptive Quantization Logic ...\nmu = torch.mean(topk_values)\nstd = torch.std(topk_values) + 1e-8\nlevels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std])\n# ... Momentum Aggregation ...\nm.view(-1)[idx].mul_(0.9).add_(val, alpha=0.1)\np.data.view(-1)[idx] -= effective_lr * m.view(-1)[idx]\n```\n\n### Next Steps\n- Monitor the `/metrics` dashboard to compare convergence speed with the new momentum-based aggregation.\n- TODO: Implement second-order momentum (Adam-style) for the outer optimizer to handle heterogeneous learning rates across Basilica nodes.\n- TODO: Explore \"Layer-wise Adaptive Density\" to prioritize communication for layers with higher gradient variance.\n\n`STATE.md` has been updated to reflect these advancements."}]},"session_id":"4c16465a-9ee1-45dd-a5a9-9da48df50adf"}

This captures the distribution of pseudo-gradients more accurately than simple sign-magnitude scaling, reducing quantization error in the Error Feedback (EF) loop.\n    - Updated `SPoTVerifier` to verify updates using statistical checks ($\\mu, \\sigma$ consistency) instead of just max-magnitude, making it harder for workers to cheat by inflating gradients.\n\n2.  **Global Outer Momentum**:\n    - Implemented a global momentum buffer in `BasilicaAggregator`. This accelerates convergence by smoothing out the sparse, asynchronous updates from heterogeneous workers.\n    - The aggregator now applies updates as $W_{t+1} = W_t - \\eta_{outer} \\cdot m_t$, where $m_t$ is the momentum-tracked sparse update.\n\n3.  **Heterogeneous Sync**:\n    - Updated `HeterogeneousSparseLoCo` to support AQ, ensuring that even workers using **Subspace Projection** (arXiv:2601.02360) benefit from more accurate gradient compression.\n\n### Updated Codebase\n\n```python:sparseloco.py\n# ... Adaptive Quantization Logic ...\nmu = torch.mean(topk_values)\nstd = torch.std(topk_values) + 1e-8\nlevels = torch.tensor([mu - 1.5*std, mu - 0.5*std, mu + 0.5*std, mu + 1.5*std])\n# ...
